      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53733143" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15156572478938838919">I had thought of L'Amour as only a Western writer and thought this to be a book about the American Indian. Very suprised that the action took place in Europe and the Middle East. Very interesting book and I would recommend it for anyone who might reject it on the bases of L'Amour's stereotyped westerns. Of coarse, any hard core L'mour fan will read it anyway.</span>

<div id="review_2008340299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2008340299" />
    <a title="A.L. Sowards" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2048362-a-l-sowards"><img alt="A.L. Sowards" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603467220p2/2048362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2008340299?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.L. Sowards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.L. Sowards" href="/user/show/2048362-a-l-sowards">A.L. Sowards</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2048362-a-l-sowards?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2048362-a-l-sowards?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2048362-a-l-sowards?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2008340299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16453983876801024073">This is my first L’Amour book, and it left me with mixed feelings. Parts were really good. And stretches made me wonder if I really wanted to keep reading it. <br/><br/>This isn’t one of L’Amour’s westerns. Instead, this is one young man’s journey across the late 12th century. The research is impressive. The character travels from the coast of Brittany, through Moorish Spain, across Europe from Paris to Kiev, then to Constantinople and a fortress in Persia. The research seemed solid, other than calling th</span>
  <span id="freeText16453983876801024073" style="display:none">This is my first L’Amour book, and it left me with mixed feelings. Parts were really good. And stretches made me wonder if I really wanted to keep reading it. <br /><br />This isn’t one of L’Amour’s westerns. Instead, this is one young man’s journey across the late 12th century. The research is impressive. The character travels from the coast of Brittany, through Moorish Spain, across Europe from Paris to Kiev, then to Constantinople and a fortress in Persia. The research seemed solid, other than calling the Byzantine Empire the Byzantine Empire (that term came later, they would have called themselves Romans) and Manual I being referred to as Manual I (I assume contemporaries would have just called him Emperor Manual). In the notes, L’Amour says he changed a few names and places to what readers were more familiar with, so I guess that’s not a complaint.<br /><br />As I said, the research was impressive, but it wasn’t always woven into the story seamlessly. Frequently the narrative stopped for a history lecture. I like history, but I prefer the info-rich stuff to come from nonfiction books, since it’s hard to trust a novel.<br /><br />The hero of the tale is Mathurian Kerbouchard, and the book is told in first person from his point of view. He’s a teenager when the book begins. He somehow knows everything there is to know about his world, and seems to be able to memorize anything he reads and then be able to write it down months later. His knowledge often strains credibility, especially for someone so young. He also manages to fall in love with six (or was it seven?) women throughout the book, all of them stunningly beautiful, of course. (FYI for those interested in the romance—none of the relationships go beyond sentence-length kisses and banter on the page. Suggestion of further activities is hinted at, but not detailed.)<br /><br />The book felt long, which was okay because it covered a lot of ground. I might have liked it better if an editor had cut out the history lectures (even though I like history) and if Kerbouchard hadn’t gotten himself into so many problems. So often he would enter a new town, insult someone, and then have it come back to bite him. Sometimes Kerbouchard was just plain arrogant (but at least he was consistent).<br /><br />This review so far isn’t very positive, but there were lots of things I enjoyed about the book. I liked the action scenes. I liked Kerbouchard’s quest to find his father (even if he seemed to be easily distracted). And for all Kerbouchard’s unrealistic knowledge, L’Amour let him get beat up enough that he didn’t come off as invincible. I also liked the underlying themes about the importance of education and I loved the yol bolsun parts. Some interesting characters made their way through the pages of the story, and the plot kept up at a good pace, other than when it slowed for historical info dumps.<br /><br />Would I recommend it? Sure. It’s a fun adventure story. Just know what you’re getting into—a story with lots of history lectures and a protagonist who is either extraordinary or unbelievable, depending on your point of view. In the author’s notes, L’Amour said he had planned to write another two books with Kerbouchard, but he died before he could accomplish that. The book ends with some closure, but not everything is tied up. So if you don’t like reading series unless you can have all the books, be aware that this series is incomplete. <br /><br />I’m giving it 3.5 stars, rounding up to 4.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16453983876801024073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11387365424377744379">It's been several years since I read this, and I need to get my hands on a new copy to read it again. I'm not a fan of Westerns, but I still know that Louis L'Amour is the undisputed king of that genre, so this story set in Medieval Europe is quite a pivot away from his comfort zone. But L'Amour is a rare talent in writing, so even writing so different from his usual craft comes easily. Featuring intrigue, revenge, a warrior-monk type protagonist, and even some real history, The Walking Drum is </span>
  <span id="freeText11387365424377744379" style="display:none">It's been several years since I read this, and I need to get my hands on a new copy to read it again. I'm not a fan of Westerns, but I still know that Louis L'Amour is the undisputed king of that genre, so this story set in Medieval Europe is quite a pivot away from his comfort zone. But L'Amour is a rare talent in writing, so even writing so different from his usual craft comes easily. Featuring intrigue, revenge, a warrior-monk type protagonist, and even some real history, The Walking Drum is a classic story, and it's one of the literary world's greatest tragedies that there is no sequel to it.</span>

<div id="review_1376310421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1376310421" />
    <a title="Trevor Parker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131205-trevor-parker"><img alt="Trevor Parker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1225840876p2/131205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1376310421?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trevor Parker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trevor Parker" href="/user/show/131205-trevor-parker">Trevor Parker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131205-trevor-parker?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131205-trevor-parker?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376310421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6910808453310259688">The themes weaving through The Walking Drum are enjoyable, consistent, and uplifting. This is the story of a boy becoming a man. And what is a man? It is a son's search for his lost father whom he refuses to believe is dead. It is of discipline and endurance being of more import than wealth or luck. And that the mind is more important than physical strength. These are some of the themes that stood out to me.<br/><br/>And there is a strong "Joseph of Egypt" feel to this book. Kerbouchard has land and a dec</span>
  <span id="freeText6910808453310259688" style="display:none">The themes weaving through The Walking Drum are enjoyable, consistent, and uplifting. This is the story of a boy becoming a man. And what is a man? It is a son's search for his lost father whom he refuses to believe is dead. It is of discipline and endurance being of more import than wealth or luck. And that the mind is more important than physical strength. These are some of the themes that stood out to me.<br /><br />And there is a strong "Joseph of Egypt" feel to this book. Kerbouchard has land and a decent life in Scotland, but fleeing from an enemy he buys passage on ship and is immediately robbed and put into slavery. He outwits his captors and earns not only his freedom, but wealth, power, and respect. Then he loses it all and ends up a prisoner. He outwits his captors and earns not only his freedom, but wealth, power, and respect. Then he loses it all and ends up a prisoner again,,, etc. I kept thinking, gee, I've read this in the bible before. It is a good story. But L'Amour does this over and over; the cycle repeats in Spain, France, Turkey, Russia...for a 12th Century man, he really gets around!<br /><br />And I finally was rolling my eyes. For mortal man, it is impressive enough to lift oneself just once from the dust and develop wealth, success, and power. Kerbouchard does it time after time after time.<br /><br />Overall, this was a tedious and melodramatic book. I felt like Kerbouchard was a 12th Century Super Hero. He could do no wrong and could beat anyone with sword, bolo, or his mind. In any discipline, he was the best. And all he had to do was smile at a woman and she would collapse into his arms in a fit of passion. Oh please!<br /><br />I would give it 2.5 stars. 2 seems a little harsh since it was well written and I did enjoy it. So I give it 3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6910808453310259688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		<td>
      
			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/18219782-looking-for-an-adventure-book">Looking for an adventure book</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c4k1EfSf4m7HCnwhg+nOPZl9M3oRKSW3Wj2dCCEYD4qZwxdEgws0ixXpTcYS40oEsXpatYcMBi0krK/lB6c/HQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z3P/rO6O51NXcU58h+a0rKFBKtDXzFSPGRkzV7vu6eeNOd35mRoxtoWSf5sW7DCViUZDH0HpdxVniAG6nVHZcA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/858.Louis_L_Amour">About Louis L&#39;Amour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/858.Louis_L_Amour"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1343675199p3/858.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/858.Louis_L_Amour">Louis L'Amour
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,085
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17707517077307795733">Louis L'Amour was an American author. L'Amour's books, primarily Western fiction, remain enormously popular, and most have gone through multiple printings. At the time of his death all 101 of his works were in print (86 novels, 14 short-story collections and one full-length work of nonfiction) and he was considered "one of the world's most popular writers".<br/>-Wikipedia</span>

</div>
</div>
